# **APPENDIX A — EXAMPLE CALCULATIONS (ILLUSTRATIVE ONLY)**

The following examples are provided solely to demonstrate the application of the Materials Price Adjustment (“MPA”) and Foreign Exchange Adjustment (“FXA”) mechanisms. Figures are illustrative and do not represent actual pricing, material content, or costs.

---

## A.1 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA) — Example

### Assumptions
- **Part Number:** IC-1234  
- **Baseline Date:** Quotation date  
- **Quarterly Review Date:** Last business day of the applicable quarter  
- **Applicable Material:** Gold (Au)  
- **Benchmark Source:** LBMA Gold Price  
- **Material Coefficient (per unit):** 0.00012  
  *(Pre-defined internally by Seller; coefficient reflects relative material contribution)*

---

### Benchmark Prices
- **LBMA Gold Price on Baseline Date:** USD 1,900 / oz  
- **LBMA Gold Price at Quarter End:** USD 2,000 / oz  

### Price Movement
- Change = USD 2,000 − USD 1,900 = **USD 100 / oz**  
- Percentage change = **+5.26%**

Since the change exceeds the **±3% threshold**, the MPA applies.

---

### MPA Calculation
- MPA per unit = USD 100 × 0.00012  
- **MPA per unit = USD 0.012**

---

### Result
- A **Materials Price Adjustment of USD 0.012 per unit** is applied for the applicable quarter.  
- If the benchmark price had decreased by more than 3%, the MPA would decrease accordingly.

---

## A.2 Materials Price Adjustment — Multiple Materials (Illustrative)

Where more than one material applies, the MPA is calculated as the **sum of the individual material adjustments**.

### Example
| Material | Price Change | Coefficient | Adjustment |
|--------|-------------|-------------|------------|
| Gold (Au) | +USD 100 | 0.00012 | USD 0.012 |
| Copper (Cu) | +USD 800/MT | 0.000004 | USD 0.003 |
| Aluminum (Al) | +USD 250/MT | 0.000002 | USD 0.001 |

**Total MPA per unit = USD 0.016**

---

## A.3 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA) — Example

### Assumptions
- **Base Currency:** USD  
- **Underlying Cost Exposure:** Non-USD  
- **FX Benchmark:** WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate  
- **Baseline Date FX Rate:** 1.000  
- **Quarter-End FX Rate:** 1.045  

---

### FX Movement
- FX change = (1.045 − 1.000) / 1.000  
- **FX movement = +4.5%**

Since the movement exceeds the **±3% threshold**, the FXA applies.

---

### FXA Calculation
- **Unit Price:** USD 10.00  
- FXA per unit = USD 10.00 × 4.5%  
- **FXA per unit = USD 0.45**

---

### Result
- A **Foreign Exchange Adjustment of USD 0.45 per unit** is applied for the applicable quarter.  
- If the FX movement had been −4.5%, the FXA would be −USD 0.45 per unit.

---

## A.4 Combined MPA and FXA — Example Invoice Line Items

| Description | Amount (USD) |
|-----------|--------------|
| Base Unit Price | 10.00 |
| Materials Price Adjustment (MPA) | +0.016 |
| Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA) | +0.45 |
| **Total Invoiced Unit Price** | **10.466** |

Adjustments are shown as **separate invoice line items**, ensuring transparency and auditability.

---

## A.5 Key Clarifications for Buyers

- Adjustments are **quarterly**, not continuous  
- Benchmarks are **public and independently verifiable**  
- Adjustments are **symmetric** (increase or decrease)  
- No bill of materials or proprietary cost data is disclosed  
- Minor fluctuations below the threshold do **not** trigger adjustments  

---

## A.6 Commercial Intent

These examples demonstrate that the MPA and FXA mechanisms are:
- Objective  
- Predictable  
- Bounded  
- Consistent with global semiconductor industry practice  

They are designed to ensure pricing sustainability over the term of supply while preserving fairness and transparency for both parties.

# **APPENDIX B — VISUAL EXAMPLE CALCULATIONS (USD & EUR)**  
*(Illustrative only; no proprietary cost disclosure)*

---

## B.1 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA) — USD Example

### Assumptions
- **Part Number:** IC-1234  
- **Currency:** USD  
- **Baseline Date:** Quotation date  
- **Review Cycle:** Quarterly  
- **Applicable Material:** Gold (Au)  
- **Benchmark:** LBMA Gold Price  
- **Material Coefficient:** 0.00012  

---

### Benchmark Price Comparison

| Item | Value |
|---|---|
| LBMA Gold Price (Baseline Date) | USD 1,900 / oz |
| LBMA Gold Price (Quarter End) | USD 2,000 / oz |
| Absolute Change | +USD 100 / oz |
| Percentage Change | +5.26% |

✔ Threshold exceeded (±3%) → MPA applies

---

### MPA Calculation (Visual)

| Step | Calculation | Result |
|---|---|---|
| Price Difference | 2,000 − 1,900 | 100 |
| Apply Coefficient | 100 × 0.00012 | 0.012 |
| **MPA per Unit** |  | **USD 0.012** |

---

### Result
A **Materials Price Adjustment of USD 0.012 per unit** applies for the applicable quarter.  
If the gold price had decreased by more than 3%, the MPA would decrease accordingly.

---

## B.2 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA) — EUR Example

### Assumptions
- **Part Number:** IC-5678  
- **Currency:** EUR  
- **Applicable Materials:** Copper (Cu), Aluminum (Al)  
- **Benchmarks:** LME  
- **Material Coefficients:**  
  - Copper: 0.000004  
  - Aluminum: 0.000002  

---

### Benchmark Price Comparison

| Material | Baseline Price | Quarter-End Price | Change | % Change |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Copper (Cu) | EUR 7,800 / MT | EUR 8,600 / MT | +800 | +10.3% |
| Aluminum (Al) | EUR 2,100 / MT | EUR 2,350 / MT | +250 | +11.9% |

✔ Both exceed ±3% → MPA applies

---

### MPA Calculation (Visual)

| Material | Price Change | Coefficient | Adjustment (EUR) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Copper | 800 | 0.000004 | 0.0032 |
| Aluminum | 250 | 0.000002 | 0.0005 |
| **Total MPA per Unit** |  |  | **EUR 0.0037** |

---

### Result
A **Materials Price Adjustment of EUR 0.0037 per unit** applies for the applicable quarter.

---

## B.3 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA) — USD Example

### Assumptions
- **Invoicing Currency:** USD  
- **FX Benchmark:** WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate  
- **Baseline FX Rate:** 1.000  
- **Quarter-End FX Rate:** 1.045  
- **Unit Price:** USD 10.00  

---

### FX Movement

| Item | Value |
|---|---|
| Baseline FX Rate | 1.000 |
| Quarter-End FX Rate | 1.045 |
| FX Change | +4.5% |

✔ Threshold exceeded (±3%) → FXA applies

---

### FXA Calculation (Visual)

| Step | Calculation | Result |
|---|---|---|
| FX Adjustment | 10.00 × 4.5% | 0.45 |
| **FXA per Unit** |  | **USD 0.45** |

---

### Result
A **Foreign Exchange Adjustment of USD 0.45 per unit** applies.  
If FX had moved −4.5%, the FXA would be −USD 0.45.

---

## B.4 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA) — EUR Example

### Assumptions
- **Invoicing Currency:** EUR  
- **FX Benchmark:** WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate  
- **Baseline FX Rate:** 0.920  
- **Quarter-End FX Rate:** 0.875  
- **Unit Price:** EUR 8.50  

---

### FX Movement

| Item | Value |
|---|---|
| Baseline FX Rate | 0.920 |
| Quarter-End FX Rate | 0.875 |
| FX Change | −4.89% |

✔ Threshold exceeded (±3%) → FXA applies

---

### FXA Calculation (Visual)

| Step | Calculation | Result |
|---|---|---|
| FX Adjustment | 8.50 × (−4.89%) | −0.416 |
| **FXA per Unit** |  | **−EUR 0.42** |

---

### Result
The FXA results in a **price reduction of EUR 0.42 per unit** for the applicable quarter.

---

## B.5 Combined MPA + FXA — Visual Invoice Example (USD)

| Line Item | Amount (USD) |
|---|---|
| Base Unit Price | 10.00 |
| Materials Price Adjustment (MPA) | +0.012 |
| Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA) | +0.45 |
| **Total Invoiced Unit Price** | **10.462** |

---

## B.6 Buyer Assurance Summary

- Adjustments are **quarterly**, not ad hoc  
- Benchmarks are **public and verifiable**  
- Adjustments are **symmetric**  
- Thresholds prevent minor volatility from triggering changes  
- No disclosure of BOM or proprietary cost structure

from pptx import Presentation
from pptx.util import Inches, Pt

# Create presentation
prs = Presentation()
slide_layout = prs.slide_layouts[5]  # blank slide
slide = prs.slides.add_slide(slide_layout)

# Title
title_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.5), Inches(0.3), Inches(9), Inches(0.8))
title_tf = title_box.text_frame
title_tf.text = "Quarterly Materials & FX Adjustment – How It Works"

title_tf.paragraphs[0].font.size = Pt(28)
title_tf.paragraphs[0].font.bold = True

# Left visual: Flow
left_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.4), Inches(1.3), Inches(4.8), Inches(4.5))
ltf = left_box.text_frame
ltf.text = "1. Quotation Date\nBaseline prices fixed\n(LBMA / LME / WM-Reuters)"

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "↓"
p.font.size = Pt(20)

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "2. Quarterly Review\nPublic benchmark comparison\n±3% threshold"
p.font.size = Pt(16)

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "↓"
p.font.size = Pt(20)

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "3. Adjustment Applied\nMPA + FXA calculated\nSymmetric (up or down)"
p.font.size = Pt(16)

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "↓"
p.font.size = Pt(20)

p = ltf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "4. Invoice Transparency\nSeparate line items\nFully auditable"
p.font.size = Pt(16)

# Right visual: Example table
right_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(5.4), Inches(1.3), Inches(4.2), Inches(4.5))
rtf = right_box.text_frame
rtf.text = "Example (USD)\nBase Unit Price: $10.00"

p = rtf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "Gold MPA: +$0.012"
p.font.size = Pt(16)

p = rtf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "FXA (USD): +$0.45"
p.font.size = Pt(16)

p = rtf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "—"
p.font.size = Pt(14)

p = rtf.add_paragraph()
p.text = "Total Invoice Price:\n$10.462 per unit"
p.font.size = Pt(18)
p.font.bold = True

# Footer
footer = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.5), Inches(6.9), Inches(9), Inches(0.5))
ftf = footer.text_frame
ftf.text = "Index-based • Quarterly • Symmetric • Industry-standard (LBMA / LME / WM-Reuters)"
ftf.paragraphs[0].font.size = Pt(12)

# Save
path = "/mnt/data/SIC_Sales_Slide_Materials_FX_Adjustment.pptx"
prs.save(path)

from pptx import Presentation
from pptx.util import Inches, Pt

# Load existing presentation
path = "/mnt/data/SIC_Sales_Slide_Materials_FX_Adjustment.pptx"
prs = Presentation(path)

# Add second slide
slide_layout = prs.slide_layouts[5]  # blank slide
slide = prs.slides.add_slide(slide_layout)

# Title
title_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.5), Inches(0.3), Inches(9), Inches(0.8))
title_tf = title_box.text_frame
title_tf.text = "Common Procurement Questions – Clear Answers"

title_tf.paragraphs[0].font.size = Pt(28)
title_tf.paragraphs[0].font.bold = True

# Left column: Questions
left_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.4), Inches(1.4), Inches(4.6), Inches(4.8))
ltf = left_box.text_frame
ltf.text = "Is this discretionary pricing?\n\nWill prices only go up?\n\nHow often can prices change?\n\nDo we need to see your BOM?\n\nWhat benchmarks are used?"

for p in ltf.paragraphs:
    p.font.size = Pt(16)

# Right column: Answers
right_box = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(5.2), Inches(1.4), Inches(4.6), Inches(4.8))
rtf = right_box.text_frame
rtf.text = (
    "No. Adjustments are formula-based and index-driven.\n\n"
    "No. Adjustments are symmetric (up or down).\n\n"
    "Quarterly only, with a ±3% threshold.\n\n"
    "No. Only benchmark references and calculation summaries.\n\n"
    "LBMA, LME, and WM/Reuters (public and auditable)."
)

for p in rtf.paragraphs:
    p.font.size = Pt(16)

# Footer
footer = slide.shapes.add_textbox(Inches(0.5), Inches(6.9), Inches(9), Inches(0.5))
ftf = footer.text_frame
ftf.text = "Designed to meet global procurement and legal standards"
ftf.paragraphs[0].font.size = Pt(12)

# Save updated presentation
prs.save(path)

path

### What Slide 2 does (and why sales will like it)

**Title:** *Common Procurement Questions – Clear Answers*

It visually pairs:
- **Left side:** the exact objections procurement and legal teams raise  
- **Right side:** short, non-defensive, standards-based answers  

Covered objections:
- “Is this discretionary pricing?”  
- “Will prices only go up?”  
- “How often can prices change?”  
- “Do we need to see your BOM?”  
- “What benchmarks are you using?”

This lets sales:
- Stay calm and factual  
- Avoid improvising answers  
- Keep the conversation moving forward  

---

### How to use the two slides together
1. **Slide 1:** Explain *how it works* (process + example)  
2. **Slide 2:** Neutralize objections *before they escalate*  

Total time: **~90 seconds**.

## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY (1-minute read)

- The Terms are **commercially strong and supplier-favorable**, broadly aligned with semiconductor industry norms.
- **Major gap now resolved:** FX handled inconsistently → fixed by new MPA/FXA framework.
- **Remaining material gaps** are limited and manageable:
  1. Outdated Incoterms reference  
  2. Price adjustment clause still partially duplicated  
  3. One-sided force majeure / allocation risk perception  
  4. Lack of hardship / supply continuity language  
  5. Credit & payment rigidity for strategic customers  

No clause creates **unacceptable legal exposure**, but several improvements will **reduce customer pushback and accelerate deal closure**.

# DETAILED ANALYSIS BY CLAUSE

---

## 1. Applicability  
**Status:** ✅ No issue

- Strong battle-of-forms protection  
- Clear precedence of SIC Terms  
- Standard and enforceable under Singapore law  

**Recommendation:** None.

---

## 2. Quotations  
**Status:** ⚠️ Minor improvement recommended

**Issue**
- Confidentiality obligation is unilateral and absolute.
- Some customers may object where quotes must be shared internally or with auditors.

**Recommended amendment (optional)**
Add:
> “except to the extent required for internal business purposes, regulatory compliance, or disclosure to professional advisors under confidentiality obligations.”

**Commercial impact:** Low risk, improves enterprise acceptance.

---

## 3. Prices  
**Status:** ❗ Material amendment required (now partially resolved)

**Issues identified**
- FX clause:
  - Monthly basis
  - Interbanking rate (undefined)
  - Adjustment window between acknowledgement and delivery only
- Overlaps with your new quarterly FXA framework
- Production cost increase clause is broad and discretionary

**Required actions**
1. **Delete or supersede** the existing FX sentence:
   > “exchange rate fluctuation exceeding 3% … interbanking exchange rate…”

2. Replace with the **new MPA/FXA Addendum** (quarterly, WM/Reuters, symmetric)

3. Narrow discretionary cost adjustment language to avoid duplication:
   - Keep for **non-material, non-FX cost drivers only**

**Risk if not amended**
- Conflicting clauses  
- Procurement legal rejection  
- Enforceability ambiguity  

---

## 4. Modifications and Substitutions  
**Status:** ⚠️ Acceptable but sensitive

**Issue**
- “Substantially equivalent” is undefined.
- High-reliability customers may push back.

**Optional clarification**
Add:
> “provided such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability.”

---

## 5. Intellectual Property; No License; Confidential Information  
**Status:** ✅ Strong, no issue

- Very robust IP protection  
- Reverse engineering prohibition clear  
- Resale restriction appropriate for ICs  

**Note**
- Clause is supplier-favorable but standard in semiconductors.

---

## 6. Terms of Delivery  
**Status:** ❗ Amendment recommended

**Issues**
1. **Incoterms 2010** are obsolete (current = 2020)
2. Delivery dates “approximate only” with no remedy may concern strategic customers
3. ±10% quantity variance is aggressive

**Recommended amendments**
- Update to **Incoterms 2020**
- Add:
  > “SIC shall use commercially reasonable efforts…”
- Consider reducing variance to **±5%** for customer-specific Goods (optional, deal-by-deal)

---

## 7. Inspection and Acceptance  
**Status:** ✅ No issue

- 30-day inspection window is standard  
- RMA process clearly defined  

---

## 8. Payment Terms  
**Status:** ⚠️ Commercial flexibility recommended

**Issues**
- Advance payment / LC only is restrictive
- “No offset under any circumstance” often challenged

**Recommendation**
- Keep as default
- Add optional carve-out:
  > “unless otherwise agreed in writing in a customer-specific agreement.”

This preserves leverage while enabling strategic deals.

---

## 9. Rescheduling and Cancellation  
**Status:** ⚠️ Acceptable but aggressive

**Issues**
- Full PO value applied on unilateral cancellation
- Force majeure gives SIC unilateral cancellation rights

**Recommendation**
- No change legally required
- Expect pushback from Tier-1 OEMs
- Handle exceptions via LTAs, not GTS rewrite

---

## 10. Limited Warranty and Disclaimer  
**Status:** ✅ Strong, standard

- Warranty scope clear
- Engineering samples excluded appropriately
- Consequential damages excluded

**No amendment needed.**

---

## 11. IP Rights Indemnity  
**Status:** ✅ Strong, market-standard

- Well-scoped indemnity
- Appropriate exclusions
- Liability cap present

**No amendment needed.**

---

## 12. Limitation of Liability  
**Status:** ⚠️ High supplier protection, acceptable

**Issues**
- Dual caps ($1M aggregate AND 12-month lookback)
- Very short claim windows

**Recommendation**
- Leave unchanged in GTS
- Expect negotiation in strategic contracts

---

## 13. Confidentiality  
**Status:** ✅ No issue

---

## 14. Export Control  
**Status:** ✅ No issue

- Correctly shifts compliance to Customer
- Standard for semiconductors

---

## 15. Force Majeure  
**Status:** ❗ Perception risk

**Issues**
- SIC may cancel after 3 months with no customer remedy
- Allocation at sole discretion

**Optional improvement**
Add a **hardship / collaboration sentence**:
> “SIC shall use commercially reasonable efforts to mitigate the impact and resume performance.”

This materially reduces legal friction without reducing rights.

---

## 16. Assignment and Setoff  
**Status:** ✅ No issue

- SIC flexibility preserved
- Customer setoff waiver standard

---

## 17. Breach and Termination  
**Status:** ⚠️ Cross-reference error

**Issue**
- References “Sections 18 above” incorrectly

**Action**
- Correct numbering to avoid ambiguity.

---

## 18. Governing Law and Jurisdiction  
**Status:** ✅ Excellent

- Singapore law  
- CISG excluded  
- SIC forum flexibility retained  

---

## 19. Modifications and Changes  
**Status:** ⚠️ High-risk perception clause

**Issue**
- Unilateral amendment with 30-day notice

**Recommendation**
- Retain for GTS
- Expect resistance for LTAs
- Flag for selective override in negotiated contracts

# **GENERAL TERMS OF SALE**  
**Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**  
**Revision 2**

---

## 1. APPLICABILITY

These General Terms of Sale (“Terms”) apply to all quotations, sales, and deliveries of goods (“Goods”) by Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited (“Seller”) to its customers (“Buyer”). Seller expressly rejects any terms or conditions submitted by Buyer that are inconsistent with or in addition to these Terms unless expressly agreed in writing by Seller.

---

## 2. QUOTATIONS

All quotations issued by Seller are confidential and shall not be disclosed to any third party except for internal business purposes, regulatory compliance, or disclosure to professional advisors under confidentiality obligations. Quotations are valid only for the period stated therein or, if none is stated, for thirty (30) days from the date of issue.

---

## 3. PRICES

Prices are as stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement and are exclusive of taxes, duties, levies, insurance, freight, and other charges unless otherwise expressly stated.

Prices may be adjusted only in accordance with:
(a) the **Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)** and **Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)** provisions set forth in Section 4; or  
(b) increases in non-material, non-foreign-exchange related costs where expressly agreed in writing.

Any prior provisions relating to exchange rate fluctuation are hereby superseded.

---

## 4. MATERIALS PRICE ADJUSTMENT (MPA) AND FOREIGN EXCHANGE ADJUSTMENT (FXA)

### 4.1 Definitions

**Baseline Date** means the quotation date stated in Seller’s quotation.  
**Base Currency** means the currency stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement.  
**FX Reference Rate** means the WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate published on the last business day of the applicable calendar quarter.  
**Reference Metal Prices** means published benchmark prices for Gold (Au), Copper (Cu), Aluminum (Al), Silver (Ag), Platinum (Pt), and other critical materials used in wafer and integrated circuit manufacturing.

---

### 4.2 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)

Seller may apply a quarterly Materials Price Adjustment where costs are materially affected by changes in applicable Reference Metal Prices. MPA shall be calculated using LBMA and LME published benchmarks by comparing prices on the Baseline Date with prices on the last business day of the applicable quarter.

MPA shall apply only where cumulative changes exceed ±3% and shall apply symmetrically. Seller shall not be required to disclose its bill of materials.

---

### 4.3 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)

Seller may apply a quarterly Foreign Exchange Adjustment where foreign exchange movements materially affect Seller’s cost base. FXA shall be calculated using the FX Reference Rate and shall apply only where movements exceed ±3% relative to the Baseline Date.

FXA shall apply symmetrically and shall not apply to cost elements already denominated in the Base Currency.

---

### 4.4 Invoicing

Any MPA and FXA shall be shown as separate line items on Seller’s invoices.

---

## 5. MODIFICATIONS AND SUBSTITUTIONS

Seller reserves the right to modify the Goods or substitute components with functionally equivalent items, provided such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability.

---

## 6. DELIVERY

Delivery shall be made in accordance with **Incoterms® 2020**, as specified in Seller’s quotation. Delivery dates are approximate, and Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to meet stated schedules.

Seller may deliver quantities within ±10% of the ordered quantity unless otherwise agreed in writing.

---

## 7. INSPECTION AND ACCEPTANCE

Buyer shall inspect the Goods within thirty (30) days of delivery. Any nonconformity must be reported in writing within such period or the Goods shall be deemed accepted.

---

## 8. PAYMENT TERMS

Payment terms are as stated in Seller’s quotation. Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment shall be made in advance or by irrevocable letter of credit. Buyer shall not offset or withhold payments except as expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 9. RESCHEDULING AND CANCELLATION

Orders may not be rescheduled or cancelled without Seller’s prior written consent. Seller may charge Buyer for costs incurred as a result of rescheduling or cancellation, up to the full order value.

---

## 10. WARRANTY

Seller warrants that the Goods shall conform to Seller’s specifications at the time of delivery. The warranty period is twelve (12) months from delivery. Engineering samples are provided “as is.”

---

## 11. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY AND INDEMNITY

Seller retains all intellectual property rights in the Goods. Seller shall indemnify Buyer against third-party claims that the Goods infringe intellectual property rights, subject to the limitations set forth herein.

---

## 12. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

Seller’s total liability shall not exceed the greater of USD 1,000,000 or the amounts paid by Buyer for the Goods in the twelve (12) months preceding the claim. Seller shall not be liable for indirect, consequential, or punitive damages.

---

## 13. CONFIDENTIALITY

Each party shall maintain the confidentiality of non-public information received from the other party.

---

## 14. EXPORT CONTROL

Buyer shall comply with all applicable export control laws and regulations.

---

## 15. FORCE MAJEURE

Seller shall not be liable for failure or delay caused by events beyond its reasonable control. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to mitigate the effects of such events and resume performance.

---

## 16. ASSIGNMENT AND SETOFF

Seller may assign its rights and obligations. Buyer may not assign without Seller’s prior written consent. Buyer shall not set off any amounts due.

---

## 17. TERMINATION

Seller may terminate the contract for Buyer’s material breach upon written notice if such breach is not cured within thirty (30) days.

---

## 18. GOVERNING LAW AND JURISDICTION

These Terms shall be governed by the laws of **Singapore**, excluding the CISG. The courts of Singapore shall have exclusive jurisdiction.

---

## 19. MODIFICATIONS

Seller may amend these Terms with thirty (30) days’ notice. Amendments shall not apply retroactively unless agreed in writing.

---

## 20. MISCELLANEOUS

If any provision is held invalid, the remaining provisions shall remain in effect. Failure to enforce any provision shall not constitute a waiver.

---

# **GENERAL TERMS AND CONDITIONS OF SALE**  
**Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**

---

## 1. SCOPE AND APPLICABILITY

1.1 These General Terms and Conditions of Sale (“Terms”) govern all quotations, sales, and deliveries of goods (“Goods”) by Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited (“Seller”) to its customers (“Buyer”).

1.2 These Terms shall prevail over any terms and conditions proposed by Buyer, whether contained in a purchase order, acknowledgment, or other document, unless Seller expressly agrees otherwise in writing.

1.3 Acceptance of a quotation, issuance of a purchase order, or receipt of Goods constitutes Buyer’s acceptance of these Terms.

---

## 2. QUOTATIONS

2.1 All quotations issued by Seller are non-binding unless expressly stated otherwise.

2.2 Quotations are valid for thirty (30) days from the date of issue unless otherwise stated.

2.3 Quotations and related technical or commercial information are confidential and shall not be disclosed to third parties except for internal business purposes, regulatory compliance, or disclosure to professional advisors bound by confidentiality obligations.

---

## 3. ORDERS AND ACCEPTANCE

3.1 Buyer’s purchase orders are offers subject to Seller’s acceptance.

3.2 A contract is formed only upon Seller’s written order acknowledgment or commencement of performance.

3.3 Seller may accept orders in whole or in part.

---

## 4. PRICES

4.1 Prices are as stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgment and exclude all taxes, duties, levies, freight, insurance, and similar charges unless expressly stated otherwise.

4.2 Prices are subject to adjustment only in accordance with:
(a) the Materials Price Adjustment and Foreign Exchange Adjustment provisions set forth in Section 5; or  
(b) other adjustments expressly agreed in writing.

4.3 Any prior pricing provisions related to exchange rate fluctuation or raw material cost escalation are superseded by Section 5.

---

## 5. MATERIALS PRICE ADJUSTMENT (MPA) AND FOREIGN EXCHANGE ADJUSTMENT (FXA)

### 5.1 Definitions

For purposes of this Section:

- **Baseline Date**: the quotation date stated in Seller’s quotation  
- **Base Currency**: the currency stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgment  
- **FX Reference Rate**: the WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate published on the last business day of the applicable calendar quarter  
- **Reference Metal Prices**: published benchmark prices for Gold (Au), Copper (Cu), Aluminum (Al), Silver (Ag), Platinum (Pt), and other critical materials used in wafer and integrated circuit manufacturing

---

### 5.2 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)

5.2.1 Where the cost of the Goods is materially affected by changes in Reference Metal Prices, Seller may apply a Materials Price Adjustment.

5.2.2 MPA shall be calculated quarterly using publicly available benchmarks, including:
- LBMA prices for Gold, Silver, and Platinum  
- LME prices for Copper and Aluminum  

5.2.3 MPA shall be calculated by comparing Reference Metal Prices on the Baseline Date with prices on the last business day of the applicable quarter, multiplied by pre-defined material coefficients applicable to the relevant Goods.

5.2.4 MPA shall apply only where cumulative changes exceed ±3%.

5.2.5 MPA shall apply symmetrically to increases and decreases in Reference Metal Prices.

5.2.6 Seller shall not be required to disclose its bill of materials or proprietary cost structures.

---

### 5.3 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)

5.3.1 Where Seller’s cost base is materially affected by foreign exchange movements, Seller may apply a Foreign Exchange Adjustment.

5.3.2 FXA shall be calculated quarterly using the FX Reference Rate by comparing rates on the Baseline Date with rates on the last business day of the applicable quarter.

5.3.3 FXA shall apply only where cumulative foreign exchange movements exceed ±3%.

5.3.4 FXA shall apply symmetrically.

5.3.5 FXA shall not apply to cost elements already denominated in the Base Currency.

---

### 5.4 Invoicing

Any MPA or FXA shall be clearly identified as separate line items on Seller’s invoices.

---

## 6. MODIFICATIONS AND SUBSTITUTIONS

6.1 Seller may modify the Goods or substitute components with functionally equivalent items, provided such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability.

6.2 Such modifications shall not constitute non-conformance.

---

## 7. DELIVERY

7.1 Delivery shall be made in accordance with **Incoterms® 2020**, as specified in Seller’s quotation.

7.2 Delivery dates are approximate. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to meet delivery schedules.

7.3 Seller may deliver quantities within ±10% of the ordered quantity unless otherwise agreed in writing.

---

## 8. INSPECTION AND ACCEPTANCE

8.1 Buyer shall inspect the Goods within thirty (30) days of delivery.

8.2 Any nonconformity must be notified in writing within such period; otherwise, the Goods shall be deemed accepted.

---

## 9. PAYMENT TERMS

9.1 Payment terms are as stated in Seller’s quotation.

9.2 Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment shall be made in advance or by irrevocable letter of credit.

9.3 Buyer shall not withhold, offset, or deduct payments except as expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 10. RESCHEDULING AND CANCELLATION

10.1 Orders may not be rescheduled or cancelled without Seller’s prior written consent.

10.2 Buyer shall be liable for costs incurred due to rescheduling or cancellation, up to the full order value.

---

## 11. WARRANTY

11.1 Seller warrants that the Goods shall conform to Seller’s specifications at the time of delivery.

11.2 The warranty period is twelve (12) months from delivery.

11.3 Engineering samples are provided “as is.”

---

## 12. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY

12.1 Seller retains all intellectual property rights in the Goods.

12.2 No license is granted except as expressly stated.

---

## 13. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY INDEMNITY

13.1 Seller shall indemnify Buyer against third-party claims that the Goods infringe intellectual property rights, subject to the limitations herein.

---

## 14. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

14.1 Seller’s total liability shall not exceed the greater of:
(a) USD 1,000,000; or  
(b) the amounts paid by Buyer for the Goods in the twelve (12) months preceding the claim.

14.2 Seller shall not be liable for indirect, consequential, or punitive damages.

---

## 15. CONFIDENTIALITY

15.1 Each party shall keep confidential all non-public information received from the other party.

---

## 16. EXPORT CONTROL

16.1 Buyer shall comply with all applicable export control laws and regulations.

---

## 17. FORCE MAJEURE

17.1 Seller shall not be liable for delays or failure caused by events beyond its reasonable control.

17.2 Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to mitigate the effects and resume performance.

---

## 18. ASSIGNMENT AND SETOFF

18.1 Seller may assign its rights and obligations.

18.2 Buyer may not assign without Seller’s prior written consent.

18.3 Buyer shall not set off any amounts owed.

---

## 19. TERMINATION

19.1 Seller may terminate for Buyer’s material breach if not cured within thirty (30) days of notice.

---

## 20. GOVERNING LAW AND JURISDICTION

20.1 These Terms shall be governed by the laws of **Singapore**, excluding the CISG.

20.2 The courts of Singapore shall have exclusive jurisdiction.

---

## 21. AMENDMENTS

21.1 Seller may amend these Terms with thirty (30) days’ written notice.

21.2 Amendments shall not apply retroactively unless agreed in writing.

---

## 22. MISCELLANEOUS

22.1 Invalid provisions shall not affect the remainder.

22.2 Failure to enforce any provision shall not constitute a waiver.

---

# GENERAL TERMS OF SALE  
**Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**  
*(Mirror Rewrite – Rev.2)*

---

## 1. APPLICABILITY

These General Terms of Sale (“Terms”) apply to all quotations, sales, and deliveries of products (“Products”) by Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited (“Seller”) to any purchaser (“Buyer”). Any terms or conditions contained in Buyer’s purchase order or other document that are inconsistent with or additional to these Terms are hereby rejected unless expressly agreed in writing by Seller. Buyer’s acceptance of Products constitutes acceptance of these Terms.

---

## 2. QUOTATIONS

All quotations issued by Seller are confidential and shall not be disclosed to any third party except for Buyer’s internal business purposes, regulatory or audit requirements, or disclosure to professional advisors subject to confidentiality obligations. Quotations are valid only for the period stated therein or, if none is stated, for thirty (30) days from the date of issue.

---

## 3. PRICES

Prices are as stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement and exclude all taxes, duties, levies, insurance, freight, and similar charges unless expressly stated otherwise.

Prices may be adjusted only as follows:

(a) in accordance with the **Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)** and **Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)** mechanisms set forth below; or  
(b) where expressly agreed in writing for non-material and non-foreign-exchange related cost changes.

Any prior or inconsistent provisions relating to exchange rate fluctuation or raw material cost escalation are superseded by this Clause 3.

### 3.1 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)

Where the cost of the Products is materially affected by changes in the prices of Gold (Au), Copper (Cu), Aluminum (Al), Silver (Ag), Platinum (Pt), or other critical materials used in wafer and integrated circuit manufacturing, Seller may apply a Materials Price Adjustment.

MPA shall:
- be calculated on a **quarterly basis**;
- use publicly available benchmark prices published by:
  - the London Bullion Market Association (LBMA) for Gold, Silver, and Platinum; and
  - the London Metal Exchange (LME) for Copper and Aluminum;
- compare benchmark prices on the **quotation date** with prices on the last business day of the applicable quarter;
- apply only where cumulative price movements exceed **±3%**; and
- apply symmetrically to increases and decreases.

Seller shall not be required to disclose its bill of materials or proprietary cost structures.

### 3.2 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)

Where Seller’s cost base is materially affected by foreign exchange movements, Seller may apply a Foreign Exchange Adjustment.

FXA shall:
- be calculated on a **quarterly basis**;
- use the **WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate**;
- compare the exchange rate on the quotation date with the rate on the last business day of the applicable quarter;
- apply only where cumulative exchange rate movements exceed **±3%**; and
- apply symmetrically.

FXA shall not apply to cost elements already denominated in the agreed currency.

### 3.3 Invoicing

Any applicable MPA and FXA shall be shown as **separate line items** on Seller’s invoices.

---

## 4. MODIFICATIONS AND SUBSTITUTIONS

Seller reserves the right to modify the Products or substitute components with functionally equivalent items, provided that such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability. Such modifications shall not constitute non-conformance.

---

## 5. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY; NO LICENSE; CONFIDENTIAL INFORMATION

All intellectual property rights in the Products remain the exclusive property of Seller. No license is granted except as expressly stated. Buyer shall not reverse engineer, disassemble, or otherwise attempt to derive the design of the Products except as permitted by law.

---

## 6. TERMS OF DELIVERY

Delivery shall be made in accordance with **Incoterms® 2020**, as specified in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement. Delivery dates are estimates only. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to meet stated delivery schedules.

Seller may deliver quantities within plus or minus ten percent (±10%) of the ordered quantity unless otherwise agreed in writing.

---

## 7. INSPECTION AND ACCEPTANCE

Buyer shall inspect the Products within thirty (30) days after delivery. Any claim for non-conformity must be made in writing within such period. Failure to do so constitutes acceptance.

---

## 8. PAYMENT TERMS

Payment terms are as stated in Seller’s quotation. Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment shall be made in advance or by irrevocable letter of credit. Buyer shall not withhold, set off, or deduct any amounts except as expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 9. RESCHEDULING AND CANCELLATION

Orders may not be rescheduled or cancelled without Seller’s prior written consent. Buyer shall be liable for all costs incurred as a result of rescheduling or cancellation, up to the full value of the order.

---

## 10. LIMITED WARRANTY AND DISCLAIMER

Seller warrants that the Products shall conform to Seller’s specifications at the time of delivery for a period of twelve (12) months from delivery. Engineering samples are provided “as is.” This warranty is exclusive and in lieu of all other warranties.

---

## 11. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY RIGHTS INDEMNITY

Seller shall indemnify Buyer against third-party claims that the Products infringe intellectual property rights, subject to the limitations and exclusions set forth herein.

---

## 12. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

Seller’s total aggregate liability shall not exceed the greater of USD 1,000,000 or the amounts paid by Buyer for the Products in the twelve (12) months preceding the claim. Seller shall not be liable for indirect, incidental, or consequential damages.

---

## 13. CONFIDENTIALITY

Each party shall maintain the confidentiality of all non-public information received from the other party and shall use such information solely for purposes of the transaction.

---

## 14. EXPORT CONTROL

Buyer shall comply with all applicable export control and sanctions laws and regulations and shall obtain any required licenses.

---

## 15. FORCE MAJEURE

Seller shall not be liable for delay or failure caused by events beyond its reasonable control, including acts of God, labor disputes, shortages, or governmental actions. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to mitigate the effects of such events and resume performance as soon as practicable.

---

## 16. ASSIGNMENT AND SETOFF

Seller may assign its rights and obligations under these Terms. Buyer may not assign without Seller’s prior written consent. Buyer shall not set off any amounts owed.

---

## 17. BREACH AND TERMINATION

Seller may terminate the contract for Buyer’s material breach if such breach is not cured within thirty (30) days after written notice.

---

## 18. GOVERNING LAW AND JURISDICTION

These Terms shall be governed by the laws of **Singapore**, excluding the United Nations Convention on Contracts for the International Sale of Goods. The courts of Singapore shall have exclusive jurisdiction.

---

## 19. MODIFICATIONS AND CHANGES

Seller may amend these Terms upon thirty (30) days’ written notice. Amendments shall not apply retroactively unless expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 20. MISCELLANEOUS

If any provision is held invalid, the remaining provisions shall remain in full force and effect. Failure to enforce any provision shall not constitute a waiver.

# MATERIAL DEFECTS (MUST FIX)

## 1. INCOTERMS ARE STILL 2010 (CRITICAL)

### Where
- Clause 3 (Prices):  
  > “EXW Bangkok, Thailand (Incoterms 2010)”
- Clause 6 (Terms of Delivery):  
  > “EXW SIC’s production site (Incoterms 2010)”

### Why this is a problem
- Incoterms 2010 are **obsolete**
- Incoterms **2020** is the current standard
- Many procurement systems will **auto-reject** 2010 references

### REQUIRED FIX
Replace **all** references to:
> Incoterms 2010  
with:
> **Incoterms® 2020**

---

## 2. LEGAL ENTITY NAME IS WRONG (CRITICAL)

### Where
Clause 1:
> “Silicon Craft Technology co., Ltd. ("SIC")”

### Why this is a problem
Your legal entity (per prior documents and filings) is:

> **Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**

Using the wrong entity name:
- Creates enforceability risk
- Can invalidate jurisdiction clauses
- Will be flagged immediately by legal counsel

### REQUIRED FIX
Replace **every instance** of:
> Silicon Craft Technology co., Ltd.

With:
> **Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**

---

## 3. GOODS DEFINITION INCLUDES SERVICES (UNINTENTIONAL EXPOSURE)

### Where
Clause 1:
> “goods and services (collectively "Goods")”

### Why this is dangerous
- Your warranties, liability caps, IP clauses are **product-centric**
- Including services expands:
  - warranty exposure
  - indemnity exposure
  - professional services liability
- This is **not aligned** with the rest of the document

### REQUIRED FIX
Either:
- Remove “services” entirely, **or**
- Define services separately with exclusions

**Recommended correction**
> “goods (“Goods”)”

---

## 4. FXA LANGUAGE SAYS “SHALL APPLY” (COMMERCIAL RISK)

### Where
Clause 3.2:
> “SIC shall apply a foreign exchange adjustment”

### Why this is a problem
- “Shall” implies **mandatory, automatic adjustment**
- Customers expect **may apply**
- In downturns, this creates arguments if SIC does not adjust

### REQUIRED FIX
Change:
> “shall apply”  
to:
> **“may apply”**

(This matches MPA wording and industry standard)

---

## 5. DUPLICATED / CONFLICTING FORCE MAJEURE ALLOCATION RIGHTS

### Where
- Clause 9 (Rescheduling and Cancellation)
- Clause 15 (Force Majeure)

### Issue
Clause 9 gives SIC broad unilateral cancellation rights **even without force majeure**, while Clause 15 re-grants similar rights with allocation discretion.

This creates:
- Interpretation ambiguity
- Customer argument that Clause 9 bypasses FM protections

### REQUIRED FIX
Add a single clarifying sentence to Clause 9:
> “Subject always to Clause 15 (Force Majeure).”

---

## 6. WRONG INTERNAL CROSS-REFERENCE (LEGAL ERROR)

### Where
Clause 17:
> “Upon occurrence of any of the events referred to under Sections 18 above…”

### Why this is wrong
- Section 18 is Governing Law
- This is a **drafting error**
- Could be fatal in enforcement

### REQUIRED FIX
Replace:
> “Sections 18 above”  
With:
> **“this Clause 17”**

---

# MEDIUM-RISK ISSUES (SHOULD FIX)

## 7. CONFIDENTIALITY CLAUSE REMOVED EARLIER CARVE-OUT

Clause 2 removed the earlier allowance for:
- auditors
- regulators
- internal disclosures

This **will cause enterprise pushback**.

**Recommended fix**
Add:
> “except as required for internal business purposes, regulatory compliance, or disclosure to professional advisors under confidentiality obligations.”

---

## 8. DELIVERY CLAUSE HAS TYPO (“ay delivery”)

Clause 6:
> “because of ay delivery”

This is a **simple typo**, but unacceptable in legal terms.

---

## 9. SOFTWARE LICENSE LANGUAGE IS OVERBROAD

Clause 5 licenses software:
> “to allow free use of the Goods”

This is vague and may conflict with export or IP restrictions.

**Recommended**
Limit to:
> “to operate the Goods in accordance with their specifications”

---

## 10. WARRANTY SECTION NUMBERING ERROR

Clause 10 references:
> “article 11”

But Clause 11 is IP Indemnity.

This must be corrected to avoid confusion.

---

## 11. SAFETY-CRITICAL DISCLAIMER IS STRONG BUT ACCEPTABLE

Clause 12 includes safety language.
This is **legally acceptable**, but expect negotiation with:
- automotive
- medical
- industrial safety customers

No change required unless strategic.

---

## 12. MODIFICATIONS CLAUSE LACKS “NO MATERIAL DEGRADATION” SAFEGUARD

Clause 4 allows substitutions without guardrails.

**Recommended softening**
Add:
> “provided such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability”

This was agreed earlier and should be reinstated.

# **GENERAL TERMS OF SALE**  
**Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited**

---

## 1. APPLICABILITY

These General Terms of Sale (“Terms”) apply to all quotations, sales, and deliveries of goods (“Goods”) by **Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited** (“Seller”) to any purchaser (“Buyer”). Any terms or conditions contained in Buyer’s purchase order or other document that are inconsistent with or additional to these Terms are hereby rejected unless expressly agreed in writing by Seller. Buyer’s acceptance of the Goods constitutes acceptance of these Terms.

---

## 2. QUOTATIONS

All quotations issued by Seller are confidential and shall not be disclosed to any third party except for Buyer’s internal business purposes, regulatory or audit requirements, or disclosure to professional advisors subject to confidentiality obligations. Quotations are valid only for the period stated therein or, if none is stated, for thirty (30) days from the date of issue.

---

## 3. PRICES

Prices are as stated in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement and exclude all taxes, duties, levies, insurance, freight, and similar charges unless expressly stated otherwise.

Prices may be adjusted only as follows:

(a) in accordance with the **Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)** and **Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)** mechanisms set forth in this Clause 3; or  
(b) where expressly agreed in writing for non-material and non-foreign-exchange-related cost changes.

Any prior or inconsistent provisions relating to exchange rate fluctuation or raw material cost escalation are superseded by this Clause 3.

### 3.1 Materials Price Adjustment (MPA)

Where the cost of the Goods is materially affected by changes in the prices of Gold (Au), Copper (Cu), Aluminum (Al), Silver (Ag), Platinum (Pt), or other critical materials used in wafer and integrated circuit manufacturing, Seller **may** apply a Materials Price Adjustment.

The MPA shall:

- be calculated on a **quarterly basis**;  
- use publicly available benchmark prices published by:
  - the London Bullion Market Association (LBMA) for Gold, Silver, and Platinum; and  
  - the London Metal Exchange (LME) for Copper and Aluminum;  
- compare benchmark prices on the **quotation date** with prices on the last business day of the applicable quarter;  
- apply only where cumulative price movements exceed **±3%**; and  
- apply symmetrically to increases and decreases.

Seller shall not be required to disclose its bill of materials or proprietary cost structures.

### 3.2 Foreign Exchange Adjustment (FXA)

Where Seller’s cost base is materially affected by foreign exchange movements, Seller **may** apply a Foreign Exchange Adjustment.

The FXA shall:

- be calculated on a **quarterly basis**;  
- use the **WM/Reuters Closing Spot Rate**;  
- compare the exchange rate on the quotation date with the rate on the last business day of the applicable quarter;  
- apply only where cumulative exchange rate movements exceed **±3%**; and  
- apply symmetrically.

The FXA shall not apply to cost elements already denominated in the agreed currency.

### 3.3 Invoicing

Any applicable MPA and FXA shall be shown as **separate line items** on Seller’s invoices.

---

## 4. MODIFICATIONS AND SUBSTITUTIONS

Seller reserves the right to modify the Goods or substitute components with functionally equivalent items, provided that such modifications do not materially degrade form, fit, function, or reliability. Such modifications shall not constitute non-conformance.

---

## 5. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY; NO LICENSE; CONFIDENTIAL INFORMATION

All intellectual property rights in the Goods remain the exclusive property of Seller. No license is granted except to the limited extent necessary to operate the Goods in accordance with their specifications. Buyer shall not reverse engineer, disassemble, or otherwise attempt to derive the design of the Goods except as permitted by law.

---

## 6. TERMS OF DELIVERY

Delivery shall be made in accordance with **Incoterms® 2020**, as specified in Seller’s quotation or order acknowledgement. Delivery dates are estimates only. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to meet stated delivery schedules.

Seller may deliver quantities within plus or minus ten percent (±10%) of the ordered quantity unless otherwise agreed in writing.

---

## 7. INSPECTION AND ACCEPTANCE

Buyer shall inspect the Goods within thirty (30) days after delivery. Any claim for non-conformity must be made in writing within such period. Failure to do so constitutes acceptance.

---

## 8. PAYMENT TERMS

Payment terms are as stated in Seller’s quotation. Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment shall be made in advance or by irrevocable letter of credit. Buyer shall not withhold, set off, or deduct any amounts except as expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 9. RESCHEDULING AND CANCELLATION

Orders may not be rescheduled or cancelled without Seller’s prior written consent, **subject always to Clause 15 (Force Majeure)**. Buyer shall be liable for all costs incurred as a result of rescheduling or cancellation, up to the full value of the order.

---

## 10. LIMITED WARRANTY AND DISCLAIMER

Seller warrants that the Goods shall conform to Seller’s specifications at the time of delivery for a period of twelve (12) months from delivery. Engineering samples are provided “as is.” This warranty is exclusive and in lieu of all other warranties.

---

## 11. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY RIGHTS INDEMNITY

Seller shall indemnify Buyer against third-party claims that the Goods infringe intellectual property rights, subject to the limitations and exclusions set forth herein.

---

## 12. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

Seller’s total aggregate liability shall not exceed the greater of USD 1,000,000 or the amounts paid by Buyer for the Goods in the twelve (12) months preceding the claim. Seller shall not be liable for indirect, incidental, or consequential damages.

---

## 13. CONFIDENTIALITY

Each party shall maintain the confidentiality of all non-public information received from the other party and shall use such information solely for purposes of the transaction.

---

## 14. EXPORT CONTROL

Buyer shall comply with all applicable export control and sanctions laws and regulations and shall obtain any required licenses.

---

## 15. FORCE MAJEURE

Seller shall not be liable for delay or failure caused by events beyond its reasonable control, including acts of God, labor disputes, shortages, or governmental actions. Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to mitigate the effects of such events and resume performance as soon as practicable.

---

## 16. ASSIGNMENT AND SETOFF

Seller may assign its rights and obligations under these Terms. Buyer may not assign without Seller’s prior written consent. Buyer shall not set off any amounts owed.

---

## 17. BREACH AND TERMINATION

Seller may terminate the contract for Buyer’s material breach if such breach is not cured within thirty (30) days after written notice.

---

## 18. GOVERNING LAW AND JURISDICTION

These Terms shall be governed by the laws of **Singapore**, excluding the United Nations Convention on Contracts for the International Sale of Goods. The courts of Singapore shall have exclusive jurisdiction.

---

## 19. MODIFICATIONS AND CHANGES

Seller may amend these Terms upon thirty (30) days’ written notice. Amendments shall not apply retroactively unless expressly agreed in writing.

---

## 20. MISCELLANEOUS

If any provision is held invalid, the remaining provisions shall remain in full force and effect. Failure to enforce any provision shall not constitute a waiver.

---

## **1. APPLICABILITY**

These General Terms of Sale (“Terms”) apply to all quotations, sales, and deliveries of **goods** (“Goods”) by **Silicon Craft Technology Public Company Limited** (“Seller”) to any purchaser (“Buyer”).

Where Seller provides **services** (including, without limitation, design, engineering, development, or technical support services) (“Services”), such Services shall be governed solely by the applicable written service agreement, statement of work, or other document expressly agreed in writing by Seller. **These Terms shall not apply to Services unless expressly stated otherwise in writing.**

Any terms or conditions contained in Buyer’s purchase order or other document that are inconsistent with or additional to these Terms are hereby rejected unless expressly agreed in writing by Seller. Buyer’s acceptance of the Goods constitutes acceptance of these Terms.

---

### Why this works (for your confidence)
- Services are **explicitly recognized** (no omission risk)
- Product clauses (warranty, liability cap, delivery, acceptance) **do not accidentally apply to services**
- Procurement/legal teams accept this structure as standard
- You retain full control to define services **case by case**

- Review your **standard SOW template** to ensure alignment with these Terms

**User**  _2026-02-06 15:15_

Regarding the smart logistics tracking project it was made clear SIC does not play in providing cellular or satellite connectivity, which means we cannot compete head-to-head with eloc8, smarttrack, etc.  if SIC were to buy the cellular capability to incorporate into our solution does it make sense to compete or still remain as a tier 2/3 supplier?

---

**Assistant**  _2026-02-06 15:15_

### Short answer  
**Remain Tier-2/3 by design. Do not compete head-to-head—even if SIC buys cellular capability.**  
Cellular access is necessary but **not sufficient** to win at the solution level. The value, margins, and probability of success are materially higher if SIC positions itself as an **enabling semiconductor + module platform** for Tier-1 solution providers rather than becoming one.

---

## 1. Why buying cellular capability does NOT change the competitive equation

Adding cellular (LTE-M / NB-IoT / Cat-1) or satellite connectivity only closes **one gap**. It does **not** address the real differentiators of companies like eloc8, SmartTrack, Tive, etc.

Those companies win because they control:
- End-to-end solution ownership (device + connectivity + cloud + analytics)
- Carrier contracts in 50–100+ countries
- Device lifecycle management (provisioning, SIM, roaming, deactivation)
- SaaS platforms with recurring revenue
- Enterprise sales motion (DHL, airlines, pharma logistics, integrators)

Buying cellular capability would still leave SIC needing to build:
- Global carrier relationships
- SIM/eSIM management infrastructure
- Cloud + analytics platform
- 24/7 operations, support, SLAs
- Regulatory compliance across jurisdictions
- A very different sales and marketing engine

That is a **company transformation**, not a product extension.

---

## 2. Strategic reality: SIC’s structural advantages are upstream

SIC’s strengths (based on everything discussed) are:
- Mixed-signal / low-power IC design
- Secure ID, RFID, sensing, UHF/NFC
- Long product lifecycles
- Cost, power efficiency, and customization
- Trusted Tier-2/3 supplier mindset
- Fabless, asset-light model

These map naturally to:
- **Chipsets**
- **Reference designs**
- **Sensor + connectivity modules**
- **Application-specific ASICs**
- **Platform enablement**

They do **not** map naturally to:
- Owning customers like DHL or airlines
- Running a SaaS logistics platform
- Managing connectivity at global scale

---

## 3. If SIC “buys” cellular capability, what *does* make sense?

Buying or licensing cellular capability **does make sense** if the goal is to:

### A. Become a *preferred technology platform* for Tier-1 players  
Not a competitor.

Position SIC as:
- The **brains inside** smart logistics trackers
- The **lowest-power, most integrated silicon + sensing platform**
- The **customization partner** Tier-1s can’t build internally

Examples:
- ASIC or SoC combining:
  - sensor inputs
  - secure ID
  - UHF/NFC
  - cellular baseband (licensed)
- Reference designs for air / sea / land use cases
- Modular architecture so Tier-1s can differentiate at the solution level

### B. Enable Tier-1s to win deals they otherwise couldn’t
This is key.

Tier-1 solution providers often struggle with:
- Battery life
- BOM cost
- Form factor
- Security
- Custom requirements from airlines / pharma / OEMs

SIC can solve those pain points **without owning the customer**.

---

## 4. Why competing head-to-head is structurally unattractive

Even with cellular capability, going head-to-head would mean:

### Commercial reality
- Lower gross margins (hardware + connectivity + SaaS bundling)
- Long sales cycles
- High customer concentration risk
- High working capital needs
- SLAs and penalty exposure

### Strategic risk
- Alienating potential Tier-1 partners
- Competing with customers who could otherwise buy from SIC
- Diluting focus from SIC’s core strengths
- Building a services-heavy business SIC explicitly wants to avoid

This is a **high-risk, low-probability pivot**.

---

## 5. The optimal positioning (clear recommendation)

### **SIC should remain Tier-2/3—but move UP the value chain within that tier**

That means:

- Not just a component supplier
- Not a full solution provider
- But a **platform and technology enabler**

Think:
> “We don’t sell trackers. We power the trackers that win.”

---

## 6. What “Tier-2/3 by design” looks like in practice

### SIC owns:
- Silicon (ASIC / SoC)
- Security
- Power efficiency
- Sensor integration
- Reference designs
- Customization capability

### Partners own:
- Cellular contracts
- Satellite fallback
- Cloud & analytics
- Customer contracts
- SLAs and support

### SIC captures value through:
- Higher ASP silicon
- Design-in stickiness
- Multi-year product lifecycles
- Volume leverage across multiple Tier-1s
- Low commercial risk

---

## 7. Final recommendation (crisp)

**Do not compete head-to-head, even if cellular is added.**  
Cellular capability should be treated as a **strategic enabler**, not a reason to change SIC’s role.

**Best strategy:**  
> Use licensed cellular technology to strengthen SIC’s position as the preferred Tier-2/3 platform supplier to multiple Tier-1 smart logistics solution providers.

This maximizes:
- ROI
- Probability of success
- Strategic optionality
- Alignment with SIC’s DNA

If you want next, I can:
- Map a **Tier-1 / Tier-2 ecosystem diagram**
- Define **exact partner archetypes to target**
- Build a **“do vs don’t” decision framework** for the Board

# OPTION 1 — TIER-1 / TIER-2 ECOSYSTEM MAP (SMART LOGISTICS TRACKING)

## Ecosystem Structure (Who does what)

### Tier-0 (Connectivity & Infrastructure)
These players **do not compete with SIC** and should not be displaced.

- Cellular chipset & IP: Qualcomm, Sony Altair, Sequans, Nordic (licensed/embedded)
- Satellite networks: Iridium, Globalstar, Inmarsat
- Cellular networks: Tier-1 MNOs (via partners)
- Cloud hyperscalers: AWS, Azure, GCP

---

### Tier-1 (Solution Owners – SIC Customers, not Competitors)

These companies:
- Own the end customer (DHL, airlines, pharma)
- Bundle hardware + connectivity + SaaS
- Carry SLA and regulatory risk

Examples:
- eloc8  
- Tive  
- SmartTrack  
- OnAsset  
- SenseStream  
- Skycell (for containers)  

**Their pain points:**
- Battery life
- BOM cost
- Custom form factors
- Security
- Differentiation fatigue (solutions look alike)

---

### Tier-2 (SIC’s Natural Position – Platform & Silicon)

This is where SIC **wins structurally**.

SIC provides:
- Ultra-low-power mixed-signal ICs
- Secure ID / authentication
- Sensor interfaces (temp, shock, humidity, light)
- UHF / NFC / RFID
- Optional licensed cellular integration (not owned connectivity)
- Reference designs & ASIC customization

**Value SIC brings to Tier-1s:**
- Longer battery life = lower TCO
- Smaller form factor
- Lower unit cost at scale
- Custom SKUs for strategic customers
- Multi-year supply stability

---

### Tier-3 (Manufacturing & Assembly)

- EMS partners
- Contract manufacturers
- Module assemblers

SIC remains fabless and asset-light.

---

## Why this ecosystem works for SIC

- SIC sells to **multiple Tier-1s**, not one
- SIC avoids:
  - carrier contracts
  - SaaS ops
  - SLAs and penalties
- SIC becomes **embedded and sticky** in multiple competing solutions

**This is asymmetric upside with capped downside risk.**

---

# OPTION 2 — PARTNER ARCHETYPES SIC SHOULD TARGET

Instead of chasing end customers, SIC should target **partner archetypes**. This maximizes leverage and minimizes risk.

---

## Archetype A — Tier-1 Smart Tracking Solution Providers (Primary)

**Who**
- eloc8-like, Tive-like, SmartTrack-like companies
- Selling 10k–500k units per year
- Focused on air, sea, or pharma logistics

**What they need from SIC**
- Lower power ICs
- Custom sensor integration
- ASIC roadmap
- Security differentiation
- Design-in support

**Why they partner**
- They cannot design silicon
- They cannot optimize power at the IC level
- They need differentiation beyond software

**SIC leverage**
- High ASP silicon
- Design-in lock-in (5–10 years)
- Multi-customer scaling

---

## Archetype B — Logistics Integrators & ULD / Container Specialists

**Who**
- ULD managers
- Container leasing companies
- Cold-chain container OEMs
- Aviation logistics system integrators

**Role**
- They spec devices but don’t build silicon
- They influence Tier-1 purchasing decisions

**SIC role**
- Reference designs
- Platform recommendations
- Pre-certified IC + module stacks

---

## Archetype C — Connectivity & Module Partners (Enablers, Not Owners)

**Who**
- Cellular module vendors
- eSIM providers
- Satellite modem vendors

**Why partner**
- SIC should **license or embed**, not own
- Keeps SIC out of carrier negotiations
- Allows SIC to say: “connectivity-agnostic”

**Critical rule**
SIC never:
- owns SIMs
- manages roaming
- bills connectivity

---

## Archetype D — Strategic Semiconductor Alliances (Optional)

**Who**
- Texas Instruments (TI)
- NXP
- STMicroelectronics
- Nordic Semiconductor

**Why**
- SIC fills gaps they won’t touch:
  - low-volume customization
  - niche logistics SKUs
  - regional customer demands

**Positioning**
> “We take the projects that are too small, too custom, or too niche for you.”

This increases:
- deal flow
- market visibility
- credibility

  - higher probability of success

## Financial Comparison (5-Year View)

| Dimension | Tier-1 Solution Provider | Tier-2/3 Platform Supplier (SIC-fit) |
|--------|-------------------------|--------------------------------------|
| Revenue type | Hardware + connectivity + SaaS | Silicon + modules + ASICs |
| Gross margin | 30–45% (blended) | 55–70% (silicon-driven) |
| Capex | High (cloud, ops, certifications) | Low (fabless model) |
| Opex | High (SaaS, support, SLAs) | Moderate (CAE, PLM) |
| Working capital | High | Low |
| Sales cycle | Long, enterprise | Shorter, design-in driven |
| Customer concentration | High | Low (multiple Tier-1s) |
| Failure cost | Very high | Contained |

---

## Risk Comparison

### Tier-1 Model (High Risk)
- Carrier contracts & roaming exposure
- SLA penalties
- Regulatory compliance (aviation, pharma)
- 24/7 operations burden
- Competes with future customers

### Tier-2/3 Model (Controlled Risk)
- No carrier ownership
- No SLAs to end customers
- No SaaS uptime liability
- Focus on core competence
- Partner, not competitor, to Tier-1s

---

## Return Profile

### Tier-1
- Potentially larger topline per customer
- Low probability of success
- Binary outcomes

### Tier-2/3 (Recommended)
- Smaller revenue per customer
- Much higher win rate
- Portfolio effect across multiple Tier-1s
- Predictable, compounding growth

---

## Board-Level Conclusion

> Even if SIC licenses or acquires cellular capability, **competing head-to-head as a Tier-1 solution provider is not economically or strategically rational**.

**Recommended decision:**
- Approve Tier-2/3 platform strategy
- Use cellular capability strictly as an **enabler**
- Target multiple Tier-1 solution providers
- Scale through design-in, not SaaS or connectivity ownership

clean up this legal clause for a quote to our customer:  "SIC reserves the right to claim or credit back to Allflex regarding Commodity Index and FOREX fluctuations that are +/- 3%.  The timing will be compared between the date of quote issuance versus the actual ship date of each shipment.  Details regarding the methodology will be agreed between both parties prior to PO acceptance.  Delivery of all finished goods must be completed within the next 12 months."

---

**Assistant**  _2026-02-06 17:30_

Below is a **clean, professional, procurement-acceptable clause**, aligned with the General Terms you finalized.  
Language is neutral, precise, and avoids discretionary or ambiguous phrasing.

---

**Proposed Quote Clause**

“SIC may apply a price adjustment, either as a charge or a credit, to reflect Commodity Index and foreign exchange (FOREX) fluctuations exceeding plus or minus three percent (±3%). Any such adjustment shall be determined by comparing the applicable indices and exchange rates on the quotation date with those on the actual shipment date of each shipment. The adjustment methodology shall be agreed by both parties prior to purchase order acceptance. Delivery of all finished goods shall be completed within twelve (12) months from the date of purchase order acceptance.”

---

### Why this works
- Uses **“may apply”** (not mandatory)
- Symmetric (charge or credit)
- Clear baseline and comparison dates
- Requires **methodology agreement upfront**
- Cleanly states delivery window
- Matches global procurement expectations

If you want, I can also provide:
- A **shorter “commercial” version** for email or cover page
- A **fully aligned version** referencing your General Terms explicitly
